        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer725701862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16764725076288371021">This book is EPIC. I loved it. LOVED it.<br/><br/>I don't think I have ever enjoyed a book so much. I find it hard to truly enjoy many books because they're so tense and frightening and every moment of them I'm worried that my favorite character will fall over dead. But there was something about Heartless that felt safe and friendly, yet full of danger and excitement--my favorite type of story. I enjoyed every minute of it. <br/><br/>I really liked the Christian aspect of the book. I could see it, but it was part o</span>
  <span id="freeText16764725076288371021" style="display:none">This book is EPIC. I loved it. LOVED it.<br /><br />I don't think I have ever enjoyed a book so much. I find it hard to truly enjoy many books because they're so tense and frightening and every moment of them I'm worried that my favorite character will fall over dead. But there was something about Heartless that felt safe and friendly, yet full of danger and excitement--my favorite type of story. I enjoyed every minute of it. <br /><br />I really liked the Christian aspect of the book. I could see it, but it was part of the story, instead of something having nothing to do with the story and just sort of thrown in there to make it "Christian", to have a moral or something. Una being like mankind and Aethelbald being like Jesus was I thought really well done and inspiring.<br /><br />Una, despite the flaws in her character, was a very likeable heroine. I didn't feel like the author was making me like her against my will like in some books I've read, I just liked her. Even when she wasn't being so good I still liked her. It was like the reader and Aethelbald are in the same shoes, liking her despite her faults.<br /><br />Aethelbald was a wonderful and flawless character. He is undoubtedly my favorite character in this book. He was so kind and awesome at the same time. He was great and I loved every second with him. :) I liked his relationship with Felix too.<br /><br />Felix was awesome. My only problem with him was that since I didn't get an age for him at first I just assumed that he was sixteen. Then it said that he was thirteen, nearly fourteen. That messed me up and I settled on him being fifteen since I couldn't see him being fourteen. But he was really cool and adorable. I loved him. He was great.<br /><br />The cat was also a great character. So mysterious and cat-like . . . only not. ;)<br /><br />I didn't think the king would be so important but I liked him. And the knights of Farthestshore were great too. I also really really liked General Argus ----<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and was so glad he wasn't killed! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The Dragon was . . . creepy. Enough said. I salute the author for making a very different villain than any I've ever read before.<br /><br />The world was so well drawn and beautiful. It felt comfortable; and fantastical and real--but not in a gross way--at the same time. I felt at home there. And the Wood seemed like a character too, which was unique and cool.<br /><br />All in all Heartless was fantastic, epic, awesome, inspiring, and a great read! Not to mention that it has one of the most beautiful covers ever. ;) This book deserves every one of the five stars I gave it and more. And now I need to get my hands on the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16764725076288371021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who loves fantasy, fairy tales, and romance.</span></div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12108421012420590844">Heartless is beautifully perfect and perfectly beautiful. The characters are colorful, lifelike, and beautifully imperfect, especially Una. There are very few characters who I've felt as close to as Una. Prince Aethelbald is also amazing- there's no way I can even begin to express how much I love him. As for the Dragon- well, I have yet to meet a villain who can equal him. The plot is deceptively simple: a princess searching for her prince and threatened by a dragon. Even a few chapters in, thou</span>
  <span id="freeText12108421012420590844" style="display:none">Heartless is beautifully perfect and perfectly beautiful. The characters are colorful, lifelike, and beautifully imperfect, especially Una. There are very few characters who I've felt as close to as Una. Prince Aethelbald is also amazing- there's no way I can even begin to express how much I love him. As for the Dragon- well, I have yet to meet a villain who can equal him. The plot is deceptively simple: a princess searching for her prince and threatened by a dragon. Even a few chapters in, though, and you'll discover that this book isn't quite what you expected- in fact, it's far better. The tale unfolds bit by bit, with the perfect blend of romance, humor, adventure, and heartbreak. It's a beautiful, inspiring, wonderful story, and a book everyone should read.</span>

  <span id="freeText12888306259927539459" style="display:none">This is a beautifully written story. <div id="review_839931686" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/839931686" />
    <a title="MC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28164369-mc"><img alt="MC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483779945p2/28164369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/839931686?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MC" href="/user/show/28164369-mc">MC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9366919-heartless">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839931686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14193291867671285012">I had seen the <i>Tales of Goldstone Wood</i> series, by Anne Elisabeth Stengl, online before, but hadn't been much interested. Then an author friend recommended the series, so I decided to pick them up. So far, I have read the first book, <i>Heartless</i>, and I am glad I did so, because it is really good.<br/><br/>As the story begins, a young prince and princess, as little children, are playing near what is believed to be an enchanted woods when they come across a dirty cat who is missing both of his eyes. The boy, F</span>
  <span id="freeText14193291867671285012" style="display:none">I had seen the <i>Tales of Goldstone Wood</i> series, by Anne Elisabeth Stengl, online before, but hadn't been much interested. Then an author friend recommended the series, so I decided to pick them up. So far, I have read the first book, <i>Heartless</i>, and I am glad I did so, because it is really good.<br /><br />As the story begins, a young prince and princess, as little children, are playing near what is believed to be an enchanted woods when they come across a dirty cat who is missing both of his eyes. The boy, Felix, doesn't think much of the very ill-looking animal, but his much more empathetic sister, Una, takes pity and carries it home with her.<br /><br />The book then cuts forward by several years, and a now teenage Una and Felix are preparing for school lessons with their tutor, when their cat Monster shows up (yes, he is the same cat as earlier mentioned). There is something special about the animal that the reader learns of about a third of the way through the novel.<br /><br />Anyways, while they are in their lessons, out of the woods, for the first time in many decades, come many fantastical creatures. Various faerie creatures, the stuff of old wives tales and legends, come tromping out for a special fair where people can buy their wares, and see and visit with these strange, scary, and delightful people. Of course, the children, lead by their father King Fidel, comes out to visit the fair, and that is where things get interesting. This is especially true when the second purpose for the people of the kingdom of Farthestshore, which is the what the kingdom of the fae is called, to visit Fidel's kingdom is revealed: Prince Aethelbald of Farthestshore wants to ask for Una's hand in marriage.<br /><br />Una rejects his proposal, as she finds him to be singularly unromantic, boring, and not at all the ideal prince of her dreams. Plus his name is boring and rhymes with “applebald”, and who can take that? Certainly Una deserves better. She finds she can't stand this uptight, stuffy, unromantic, <i>unwanted</i> suitor. For those who wonder, yes, this is very much her attitude.<br /><br />Upset at being jilted, but still intending to woo her over, and concerned about her welfare, the prince of Farthestshore leaves on an errand, but intends to return as soon as possible. It should be noted that he is not trying to stalk her or refuse her answer of “no” in a bad way. He simply knows some of the evil that is about to happen to her kingdom, and is determined to prevent it. He tries to warn King Fidel before he leaves, but Fidel ignores his warnings, much to his later regret.<br /><br />While Aethelbald is gone, tragedy strikes and the kingdom is attacked by a dragon and an enemy army. And the dragon has a dark secret in store for Una, one that will transform her life into a nightmare. The royal family is spread to the winds, and their only hope lies in a man whom Una has treated despicably.<br /><br />For those who think I shared too many spoilers so far, I am sorry. I felt that just saying that a dragon attacked and the jilted suitor had to save them all wasn't a good enough description. Unless the background is understood, the main plot, which I have left many details unexplained about, can not be properly grasped.<br /><br />This book was oh so beautifully written. Stengl's use of language was riveting and absolutely poetic. It wasn't overly done, though. There was no “purple prose” here, just language that fit each situation wonderfully, yet had a lovely sort of “ring” to it. This was good, as it made the second half of the novel, where the main characters undergo a <i>lot</i> of suffering, more bearable. The almost whimsical tone of the words was a reminder that, despite the bad stuff happening at that moment, this isn't a super dark story, and that good will win in the end.<br /><br />Though very little in the way of the religion of this fictional world comes into play in this book (what happens in later books I don't know <i>yet</i>), there are some obvious (at least to me, they are) parallels to Christian theology. I can easily see Aethelbald as having many traits of a Messianic archetype. Even when rejected and treated horribly, he still sacrifices all for others, including in a physical/metaphysical sense I still don't understand, his heart. He loves Una as he is commanded by his father to do so. Una has to suffer some things as Aethelbald saves her from her crisis and her dark secret. The thing is that I could be entirely wrong, but even if I'm right, the ideas are subtle enough that one will not notice them if one doesn't think about it. In other words, this isn't “in your face” preaching, but subtle moral points.<br /><br />The above gets into why I don't have much to criticize about this book. When I read it, for most of the book, before I saw the various thematic elements of the story, I really disliked Una and wanted nothing to do with the parts of the story where she was the point of view character. She had empathy for those weaker than herself and she believed in others, but that is about all I can say good about her. For the most part, as noted in my description of her thoughts in an earlier paragraph, she was an absolutely spoiled, arrogant brat. Not mean, but still as spoiled and arrogant as a person can be and still be called at all “nice”.<br /><br />I honestly wondered what in the world Aethelbald could see in her to love, until the story progressed and the various revelations of the backstory and of the prince of Farthestshore's feelings and character came to light. When they did so, I saw that the way she was written was on purpose to make this point about how only the sacrifice of Another can take away our hurts. We don't deserve Christ's sacrifice, as we are unlovely, but He gave all and rose for us to save us nonetheless.<br /><br />The one single part I didn't like was how abrupt the ending was. While I thought that the ending of some books, like Jill Williamson's <i>From Darkness Won</i>, for instance, are arguably too long and drawn out, this one was too fast and didn't give the reader enough of a “payoff” in terms seeing the characters getting to be happy post-victory.<br /><br />This book was so, so, <i>soooooo</i> beautifully-written, convicting, and a great page-turner. I can't recommend it enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14193291867671285012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_476420525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476420525" />
    <a title="Carmel Elizabeth " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11614511-carmel-elizabeth"><img alt="Carmel Elizabeth " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545428858p2/11614511.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476420525?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmel Elizabeth " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmel Elizabeth " href="/user/show/11614511-carmel-elizabeth">Carmel Elizabeth </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476420525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2699956466303095060">The only fantasy I have read before this book was C.S. Lewis and a little Tolkien. But with the persuasion of two respected blog friends and a determined sister, I picked it up. (Okay, so I actually got the series for Christmas. But hush, those are meaningless details.)<br/><br/>My first thought was "I really like this writing style." But that was before I was swept into Anne Elisabeth Stengl's marvelous world of allegory. Have I ever mentioned that I really like allegory? Well, now you know. <br/><br/>In reading s</span>
  <span id="freeText2699956466303095060" style="display:none">The only fantasy I have read before this book was C.S. Lewis and a little Tolkien. But with the persuasion of two respected blog friends and a determined sister, I picked it up. (Okay, so I actually got the series for Christmas. But hush, those are meaningless details.)<br /><br />My first thought was "I really like this writing style." But that was before I was swept into Anne Elisabeth Stengl's marvelous world of allegory. Have I ever mentioned that I really like allegory? Well, now you know. <br /><br />In reading some reviews before I read the book, I've heard several people say that Una bothered them; she was too silly and somewhat ditsy. But I found this to further the allegory. I see Una as representing us as humans, and her ridiculous nature (which was not as much as it was made out to be) representing our own petty way of life. Had Princess Una been a strong heroine with a razor-sharp wit, that would be ill delineation of the human race.<br /><br />In conclusion, well done Miss Stengl. Your book has quickly made it's way to my list of favorites, and I look forward to reading more of your work. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2699956466303095060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_973709538" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/973709538" />
    <a title="Lindsey (Books for Christian Girls)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19266895-lindsey-books-for-christian-girls"><img alt="Lindsey (Books for Christian Girls)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540926238p2/19266895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/973709538?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey (Books for Christian Girls)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey (Books for Christian Girls)" href="/user/show/19266895-lindsey-books-for-christian-girls">Lindsey (Books for Christian Girls)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19266895-lindsey-books-for-christian-girls?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer973709538" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6892586708913672401">About this book:<br/><br/> <i>“The Dragon King Seeks His Princess—<br/> Who Dares to Stop Him?<br/> Princess Una of Parumvir has come of age and will soon marry. She dreams of a charming prince, but when her first suitor arrives, he's not what she'd hoped. Prince Aethelbald of mysterious Farthestshore has travelled a great distance to prove his love--and also to bring hushed warnings of danger. A dragon is rumored to be on the hunt and blazing a path of terror. <br/> Una, smitten instead with a more dashing prince, refuses</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6892586708913672401" style="display:none">About this book:<br /><br /> <i>“The Dragon King Seeks His Princess—<br /> Who Dares to Stop Him?<br /> Princess Una of Parumvir has come of age and will soon marry. She dreams of a charming prince, but when her first suitor arrives, he's not what she'd hoped. Prince Aethelbald of mysterious Farthestshore has travelled a great distance to prove his love--and also to bring hushed warnings of danger. A dragon is rumored to be on the hunt and blazing a path of terror. <br /> Una, smitten instead with a more dashing prince, refuses Aethelbald's offer--and ignores his cautions with dire consequences. Soon the Dragon King himself is in Parumvir and Una, in giving her heart away unwisely, finds herself in his sights. Only those courageous enough to risk everything have a hope of fighting off this advancing evil.”</i><br /><br /><br />Series: Book #1 of the <i>“Tales of Goldstone Wood”</i> series.<br /><br /><br />Spiritual Content- This is an Allegory. More in the Final Thoughts.<br />*Note: a <i>“ugly as sin”</i>, a <i>“devil’s carnival”</i> and a <i>“Go to the hell prepared for you”</i>; Fortune reading; Mentions of sacrifices.<br /><br /><br />Negative Content- Minor cussing including: a ‘biddy’, two ‘stupid’s, two ‘wench’s, three forms of ‘idiot’; Many curses are said but not written; Nightmares (semi-detailed); Dragons &amp; fighting (semi-detailed to detailed); Blood (up to semi-detailed); Dead people (barely-above-not-detailed); Mentions of hunting dogs &amp; dead dogs; Mentions of drinking &amp; wine; Mentions of gambling.<br /><br /><br />Sexual Content- a barely-above-not-detailed kiss and a barely-above-not-detailed forehead kiss; Many, many, many mentions of marriage, suits &amp; romance; A mention of a dragon mating and laying an egg (but that’s not where dragons come from); A little bit of Love, falling in love, &amp; the emotions. <br /><br />-Princess Una, 18<br /> P.O.V. mainly of Una’s (but a few others as well) <br /> 363 pages<br /><br />~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*<br />Pre Teens- One Star <br />New Teens- One Star (and a half)<br />Early High School Teens- Three Stars <br />Older High School Teens- Four Stars <br />My personal Rating- Three Stars (and a half)<br />Before I read this book I knew three things about it: it’s an Allegory/fantasy, has dragons and the fandom has really interesting drawings! Now, three confessions:<br />1.)	This was my first time reading an allegory. (I’ve never read the Narnia series, I know, I know, I should, but I’m just not one for mythical creatures.) {Read the Allegory <a href="http://oliviakfisher.blogspot.com/2014/10/tales-of-goldstone-wood-allegory.html" rel="nofollow noopener">theory that I referred to for this book Here!}</a><br />2.)	I’m not big on dragons, so this was <i>very</i> interesting! <s>Plus that the dragons were evil?!</s> And seeing all the fan drawings from this series made me wonder just <i>what</i> is in this series! (Really interesting fandom this series has! ;) )<br />3.)	I actually enjoyed this novel! I went in curious and wondering about how the Allegory plays in and turned out liking it. Is anyone a teeny bit shocked? :)<br /><br /><i>“Heartless”</i> was different and a little weird (keep in mind that I’m normally into Historicals) but it was a good different and weird. I’m looking forward to reading the rest of the series and possibly joining the fan base. We’ll see. ;)<br /><br /><br />Link to review:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://booksforchristiangirls.blogspot.com/2015/06/heartless-by-anne-elisabeth-stengl.html">http://booksforchristiangirls.blogspo...</a><br /> <br /><br />*BFCG may (Read the review to see) recommend this book by this author. It does not mean I recommend all the books by this author.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1808980036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1808980036" />
    <a title="Boundless" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56656165-boundless"><img alt="Boundless" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465992677p2/56656165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1808980036?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Boundless" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Boundless" href="/user/show/56656165-boundless">Boundless</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56656165-boundless?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1808980036&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1808980036" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8444193990187092966">Content Rating: G<br/><br/>--Original Review Below--<br/>I'm starting to like writing pros and cons lists for my reviews, so let me write some here:<br/>Pros:<br/>- JESUS. Well, what I mean is that this is a Christian allegory. Keeping this in mind really enriches the plot and characters, and made me think about Christ's love for humanity in a different way.<br/>- Above decent writing. IMO, Christian fiction is usually not written very well, but this book made me rethink just how well the writing can be in good Christian fic</span>
  <span id="freeText8444193990187092966" style="display:none">Content Rating: G<br /><br />--Original Review Below--<br />I'm starting to like writing pros and cons lists for my reviews, so let me write some here:<br />Pros:<br />- JESUS. Well, what I mean is that this is a Christian allegory. Keeping this in mind really enriches the plot and characters, and made me think about Christ's love for humanity in a different way.<br />- Above decent writing. IMO, Christian fiction is usually not written very well, but this book made me rethink just how well the writing can be in good Christian fiction. Granted, it's not on the level of the world's greatest YA storytellers, but it worked for the story the book was trying to tell.<br />- You feel for the characters. I actually cared about Una, the MC, to the point that I actually, literally started crying near the end. No book has made me actually tear up before. EVER. I attribute the fact that I cared to the allegorical nature of the book: Una, representing humanity / the Church, becomes the Christian reader. Thus, when Una feels lost, I remembered when I felt lost, and when she finds out that she needed the Prince of Farthestshore all along, I remembered when I needed Christ's love.<br />- Not too strict an allegory. This could be a pro or a con, I guess, depending on where the series goes.<br />Cons:<br />- Cliches. They're not too problematic in a Christian allegory, but as a reader they were slightly annoying.<br />- Switching POV too quckly. I enjoyed Una's POV the most, so switching to others' POVs, such as her brother's or father's, was a little irritating. Luckily, the book went quickly in these parts, so I could get back to Una's POV in no time.<br />- Didn't wrap up all the loose ends. I guess this could be because it's a series, and will wrap up the subplots later. I especially wanted to know about Sir Eanrin, but oh well.<br />- I have no desire to finish this series. This statement sounds like a contradiction to my previous statement, but it really isn't. While I'm curious about what happened to Sir Eanrin and Prince Lionheart, I cared about Princess Una and Prince Aethelbald the most. Their story is finished now, wrapped up completely in a satisfying ending. Since that is the plot thread I cared about the most, I have very little interest in the rest of the series. So I guess this is a personal problem I had with the book, which others probably won't see.<br />Verdict: I loved this book more than I thought I would. It has renewed my interest in Christian fantasy books. Before reading this, I thought the Chronicles of Narnia were the only good Christian fantasy, but now I realize that there's many Christian fantasy books without recognition that could possibly be worth my time, if only I dared to look. Which I will now.<br />However, the book feels like it should be a standalone and not the first in a series, despite the subplots not being wrapped up. A little bit of hard-to-follow writing as well make this book four stars and not five. But coming from a person who's trying hard not to give out too many five star ratings, this is still a great score for a book I probably would never have picked up without the recommendation from Tracey Dyck. So thank you, Tracey, for recommending this beautiful book to me. I can safely say that it's the first that ever made me literally cry, which is a huge, HUGE plus IMO. Thank you for waiting patiently for nearly a month for me to finish it, lol! God bless, and remember, Jesus loves you more than anyone else can, including yourself!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8444193990187092966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8422893853192607932">Princess Una has just come of age, and is expecting suitors to start lining up at her door immediately. However, the first prince who comes calling is so contrary to her imagined perfect prince and visions of romance that she rebuffs his offer of marriage without even considering the man who is asking.<br/><br/>When rumors of something terrible and dangerous that has taken over a neighboring kingdom start to reach the ears of Una and her family, the spoiled princess does not dream that these whispers coul</span>
  <span id="freeText8422893853192607932" style="display:none">Princess Una has just come of age, and is expecting suitors to start lining up at her door immediately. However, the first prince who comes calling is so contrary to her imagined perfect prince and visions of romance that she rebuffs his offer of marriage without even considering the man who is asking.<br /><br />When rumors of something terrible and dangerous that has taken over a neighboring kingdom start to reach the ears of Una and her family, the spoiled princess does not dream that these whispers could have anything to do with her. Wrapped up in her own concerns, Una does not realize she is in danger until it is far too late.<br /><br />Can true love really conquer all?<br /><br /><br />I really enjoyed this story. It is what might be considered an "original fairy tale" - not really fantasy, not a re-telling, but a story set in a fairy tale world with fairy tale type characters. And while I love classic, epic fantasy, I must confess that I have a soft spot for fairy tales. Particularly original ones, though retellings are wonderful as well.<br /><br />There is also a hint of allegory to this tale, that I really loved. Thankfully, I did not feel that the allegory jumped out and smacked me across the face, nor did I feel that the story got sacrificed for the sake of the allegory - which is far too often the case in the Christian Fantasy genre.<br /><br />This story has it all: princesses, knights, princes, dragons, sword-fights, ballads, romance, betrayal, jesters, and a blind cat (who is far more than he seems).<br /><br />I give it 5/5 stars. If you enjoy fairy tales, or just love a good villainous dragon... I highly recommend this book. (And the rest of the series... I'll post my reviews of the rest of the books later).</span>

<div id="review_348390531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348390531" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1707809-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546319248p2/1707809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348390531?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1707809-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1707809-jennifer?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1707809-jennifer?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1707809-jennifer?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1707809-jennifer?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348390531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer767514040150685042">It's not often that I come across a book that I really couldn't stand to read (of course, most of the time it's because I'm able to flip to the end - with my Kindle, unfortunately, I had to read through it if I wanted to know the ending). Unfortunately, "Heartless" falls into this category. <br/><br/>None of the characters were likable, especially Princess Una. She was rude, shallow, and juvenile, with absolutely no redeeming qualities. She's not very intelligent, courageous, or kind, and this doesn't cha</span>
  <span id="freeText767514040150685042" style="display:none">It's not often that I come across a book that I really couldn't stand to read (of course, most of the time it's because I'm able to flip to the end - with my Kindle, unfortunately, I had to read through it if I wanted to know the ending). Unfortunately, "Heartless" falls into this category. <br /><br />None of the characters were likable, especially Princess Una. She was rude, shallow, and juvenile, with absolutely no redeeming qualities. She's not very intelligent, courageous, or kind, and this doesn't change throughout the entire book. For this reason, I have no idea what Prince Aethelbald was so in love with her. Aethelbald himself could have been such a great character, but instead was reduce to a somewhat bland personality. The evil Dragon King was fairly one dimensional too, and both Una's father and brother were not very interesting (the brother was somewhat of a whiny brat, to be honest).<br /><br />The plot itself was okay, but there were things that are brought up but never mentioned again or explained. It annoys me when authors throw in seemingly important hints but then never bother to fully address them later on, and unfortunately, this happens quite a lot in Heartless, both with plot and with other characters. <br /><br />I would have a very hard time recommending this book to anyone. Una ruined the book for me, and unfortunately, the plot couldn't redeem her character. <br /><br />Note: Apparently, this book was a giant Christian allegory. I found this out after I had already written my review, so I'd like to put in a disclaimer that my rating and review have nothing to do with my personal beliefs. </span>
  <a data-text-id="767514040150685042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_608117719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/608117719" />
    <a title="Ashlee Willis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14060160-ashlee-willis"><img alt="Ashlee Willis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546292487p2/14060160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/608117719?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashlee Willis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashlee Willis" href="/user/show/14060160-ashlee-willis">Ashlee Willis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14060160-ashlee-willis?shelf=fantasy-favorites">fantasy-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer608117719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer667440883161433007">A lovely, gently-told fairytale with a classic, powerful truth at heart. Stengl's style is both flowing and attention-grabbing, making this book such a quick and easy read. I couldn't seem to put it down, myself :)<br/><br/>It's a fantasy with a princess, prince, knights and dragons... All the classic elements are there, but there is such a refreshing and NEW feel to it, and there's a much deeper meaning beneath for those who care to see it, making it a tale that will stay with you long after you've put t</span>
  <span id="freeText667440883161433007" style="display:none">A lovely, gently-told fairytale with a classic, powerful truth at heart. Stengl's style is both flowing and attention-grabbing, making this book such a quick and easy read. I couldn't seem to put it down, myself :)<br /><br />It's a fantasy with a princess, prince, knights and dragons... All the classic elements are there, but there is such a refreshing and NEW feel to it, and there's a much deeper meaning beneath for those who care to see it, making it a tale that will stay with you long after you've put the book down.<br /><br />A story I would recommend to everyone I know! Loved it, loved it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="667440883161433007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b9sRDrInlExj1upkeN953p424zYqNP6FX48C5BrX4VFruxRau6RcnKUBAQZPx3YLjMQwmuMUU4OgZOVHsBwDgw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BtzahCeHV6NA3rz1pLUj19vnxSYsAgw+QK5l1x8St58CvN/QLgSfc4YJV5eTrSwCyRUWiuUioTi/RYJ0tdlVTQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer12138169888326039419">Anne Elisabeth Stengl makes her home in Raleigh, North Carolina, where she lives with her husband, Rohan, a passel of cats, and one long-suffering dog. When she's not writing, she enjoys Shakespeare, opera, and tea, and studies piano, painting, and pastry baking. She studied illustration at Grace College and English literature at Campbell University. She is the author of the TALES OF GOLDSTONE WOO</span>
  <span id="freeText12138169888326039419" style="display:none">Anne Elisabeth Stengl makes her home in Raleigh, North Carolina, where she lives with her husband, Rohan, a passel of cats, and one long-suffering dog. When she's not writing, she enjoys Shakespeare, opera, and tea, and studies piano, painting, and pastry baking. She studied illustration at Grace College and English literature at Campbell University. She is the author of the TALES OF GOLDSTONE WOOD, which currently includes seven novels and two novellas, with plenty more works due to release over the next few years. Her novels HEARTLESS, VEILED ROSE, and DRAGONWITCH have each been honored with a Christy Award, and STARFLOWER was voted winner of the 2013 Clive Staples Award.</span>
